<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">NEW YORK, July&nbsp;23, 2015 &#150; Lazard Ltd (NYSE: LAZ) today reported record second-quarter operating revenue<SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1</SUP> of $607 million, and net income, as adjusted<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1</SUP>, of $130 million for the quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2015. Net income per share, as adjusted<SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1</SUP>, was $0.98 (diluted) for the quarter, excluding a net benefit of $237 million, or $1.78 per share (diluted), related to a release of the valuation allowance on deferred tax assets<SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">2</SUP>, compared to $0.64 (diluted) for the 2014 second quarter. Pre-tax income per share (diluted), as adjusted<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1</SUP>, was 37% higher than the second quarter
of 2014. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Record first-half 2015 operating revenue<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1</SUP> of $1,188 million resulted in net income, as
adjusted<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1</SUP>, of $233 million, or $1.75 per share (diluted), excluding the second-quarter net benefit<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">2</SUP> and the first-quarter debt refinancing
charge<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">4</SUP>. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Second-quarter 2015 net income on a U.S. GAAP basis was $374 million, or $2.82 (diluted)
per share, including the second-quarter net benefit<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">2</SUP>. First-half 2015 net income on a U.S. GAAP basis was $430 million, or $3.23 (diluted) per share, including the second-quarter net benefit and
the first-quarter debt refinancing charge<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">4</SUP>. A reconciliation of our U.S. GAAP results to the adjusted results is presented on page 19 of this press release. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;Lazard continues to gain momentum, with record revenues for the second quarter and first half in an uneven macroeconomic environment,&#148; said Kenneth
M. Jacobs, Chairman and Chief Executive Officer of Lazard. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;Both our businesses are in excellent position. Lazard is the only advisory-focused firm
with the global scale, and breadth and depth of expertise, to manage large, complex transactions across every sector. Our Asset Management franchise continues to build on its global investor base and expand its investment solutions for our
clients,&#148; said Mr.&nbsp;Jacobs. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;Our strong results reflect the operating leverage of our business and our continued discipline on costs,&#148;
said Matthieu Bucaille, Chief Financial Officer of Lazard. &#147;We remain focused on profitable revenue growth, investment in our businesses and the return of capital to shareholders.&#148; </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>OPERATING REVENUE </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><U>Financial Advisory </U></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>In the text portion of this press release, we present our Financial Advisory results as Strategic Advisory and Restructuring. Strategic Advisory includes 1)
M&amp;A and Other Advisory (Other includes Capital Advisory and Sovereign Advisory) and 2) Capital Raising (includes Capital Markets Advisory and Private Fund Advisory). </I></P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">2 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Second Quarter </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Financial Advisory operating revenue was a second-quarter record of $316 million, 13% higher than the second quarter of 2014. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Strategic Advisory operating revenue was a second-quarter record of $290 million, 12% higher than the second quarter of 2014. The increase was primarily
driven by M&amp;A and Other Advisory revenue of $273 million, also a second-quarter record and 17% higher than the second quarter of 2014. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the
second quarter of 2015, Lazard remained engaged in highly visible, complex M&amp;A transactions and other strategic advisory assignments, including cross-border transactions, distressed asset sales, and capital structure and sovereign advisory, in
the Americas, Europe, Africa, Asia and Australia. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Among the major M&amp;A transactions that were completed during the second quarter of 2015 were the
following (clients are in italics): <I>Reynolds American (RAI)</I> in its $27.4 billion acquisition of Lorillard and $7.1 billion sale of selected brands and assets to Imperial Tobacco, and the $4.7 billion investment in RAI by British American
Tobacco; <I>The Zeppelin-Stiftung Foundation</I> in ZF Friedrichshafen&#146;s $13.5 billion acquisition of TRW Automotive; <I>Integrys Energy Group&#146;s</I> $9.1 billion sale to Wisconsin Energy; <I>Alexion Pharmaceutical&#146;s</I> $8.4 billion
acquisition of Synageva; <I>Siemens&#146;</I> $7.8 billion acquisition of Dresser-Rand; and <I>Toll Holdings&#146;</I> A$8.0 billion sale to Japan Post. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In Capital Advisory, we continued to provide advice regarding balance sheet issues to public and private clients globally, including: <I>NJJ Capital/Orange
Switzerland</I> on its CHF 2.0 billion debt refinancing; <I>SPIE</I> on its &#128;1.0 billion IPO; <I>Univar</I> on its $770 million IPO; and <I>LondonMetric Property</I> on its &pound;400&nbsp;million refinancing. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Our Sovereign Advisory business remained active worldwide, including assignments in <I>Greece</I> and <I>Ukraine</I>. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Restructuring operating revenue of $26 million was 24% higher than the second quarter of 2014, reflecting the closing of large assignments. During and since
the second quarter of 2015 we have been engaged in a broad range of highly visible and complex restructuring and debt advisory assignments including a number in the energy sector, such as: <I>Longview Power, Sabine Oil&nbsp;&amp; Gas, </I>the
<I>Official Committee of Unsecured Creditors </I>of Energy Future Holdings and <I>creditors </I>of Walter Energy in connection with their Chapter 11 bankruptcies; and <I>Hercules Offshore</I> on its capital structure. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Please see a more complete list of M&amp;A transactions on which Lazard advised in the second quarter, or continued to advise or completed since
June&nbsp;30, 2015, as well as Capital Advisory, Sovereign Advisory and Restructuring assignments, on pages 8 -11 of this release. </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>First Half
</U></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Financial Advisory operating revenue was a first-half record of $618 million, 11% higher than the first half of 2014. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">3 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Strategic Advisory operating revenue was a first-half record of $569 million, 13% higher than the first half of
2014. The increase was primarily driven by M&amp;A and Other Advisory revenue of $534 million, also a first-half record and 13% higher than the first half of 2014. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Lazard advised or continues to advise on a number of significant and complex M&amp;A transactions announced year to date, including: <I>Heinz&#146;s</I>
combination with Kraft Foods, valuing the new entity at $115 billion; <I>The Mylan Stichting </I>on the $43 billion unsolicited expression of interest in Mylan by Teva; <I>Aetna&#146;s</I> $37.0 billion acquisition of Humana; <I>Delhaize&#146;s</I>
&#128;31.0 billion merger with Ahold; <I>RockTenn&#146;s</I> $21.0 billion merger with MeadWestvaco; and <I>The Williams Companies</I> in its review of strategic alternatives. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Restructuring operating revenue was $49 million for the first half of 2015, 4% lower than the first half of 2014. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><U>Asset Management </U></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Second Quarter </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Asset Management operating revenue was a second-quarter record of $290 million, 2% higher than the second quarter of 2014. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Management fees were a second-quarter record of $258 million, slightly above the second quarter of 2014, and 3% higher than the first quarter of 2015,
primarily reflecting changes in average AUM. Incentive fees during the period were $7 million, compared to $16 million in the second quarter of 2014. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Average AUM for the second quarter of 2015 was a record $203 billion, 2% higher than the average AUM in both the second quarter of 2014 and the first quarter
of 2015. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">AUM as of June&nbsp;30, 2015, was $203 billion, a 1% decrease from June&nbsp;30, 2014. AUM increased 2% from March&nbsp;31, 2015, primarily
driven by net inflows and foreign exchange adjustments. Net inflows of $1.6 billion were primarily driven by a broad range of equity and fixed-income strategies. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>First Half </U></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Asset Management operating revenue was a
first-half record of $561 million, 2% higher than the first half of 2014. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Management fees were a first-half record of $510 million, 3% higher than the
first half of 2014, primarily reflecting changes in average AUM. Incentive fees were $13 million in the first half of 2015, compared to $26 million in the first half of 2014. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Average AUM for the first half of 2015 was $201 billion, 5% higher than the first half of 2014. Net inflows were $2.6 billion for the first half of 2015. </P>

 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">4 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>OPERATING EXPENSES </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><U>Compensation and Benefits </U></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>In managing
compensation and benefits expense, we focus on annual awarded compensation (cash compensation and benefits plus deferred incentive compensation with respect to the applicable year, net of estimated future forfeitures and excluding charges). We
believe annual awarded compensation reflects the actual annual compensation cost more accurately than the GAAP measure of compensation cost, which includes applicable-year cash compensation and the amortization of deferred incentive compensation
principally attributable to previous years&#146; deferred compensation. We believe that by managing our business using awarded compensation with a consistent deferral policy, we can better manage our compensation costs, increase our flexibility in
the future and build shareholder value over time. </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">For the second quarter of 2015, we accrued compensation expense at an adjusted GAAP compensation
ratio of 55.6%. This resulted in $337 million of adjusted GAAP compensation and benefits expense<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1</SUP>, approximately even with the second quarter of 2014. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">For the first half of 2015, we accrued compensation expense at an adjusted GAAP compensation ratio of 55.6%. This resulted in $661 million of adjusted GAAP
compensation and benefits expense<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1</SUP>, 1% higher than the first half of 2014. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The adjusted GAAP
compensation ratios of 55.6% for the second quarter and first half of 2015 were consistent with the full-year 2014 ratio and compared to 58.8% for the second quarter and first half of 2014. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Our goal remains to grow awarded compensation expense at a slower rate than revenue growth, and to achieve a compensation-to-operating revenue ratio over the
cycle in the mid- to high-50s percentage range on both an awarded and adjusted GAAP basis, with consistent deferral policies<I>.</I> </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><U>Non-Compensation Expense </U></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">For the second quarter
of 2015, adjusted non-compensation expense<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1,2</SUP> was $110 million, 2% lower than the second quarter of 2014. The ratio of adjusted non-compensation expense to operating revenue for the second quarter
of 2015 was 18.1%, compared to 19.5% for the second quarter of 2014. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">For the first half of 2015, adjusted non-compensation expense<SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1,2</SUP> was $216 million, 1% higher than the first half of 2014. The ratio of adjusted non-compensation expense to operating revenue for the first half of 2015 was 18.2%, compared to 19.3% for the first
half of 2014. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Our goal remains to achieve an adjusted non-compensation expense-to-operating revenue ratio over the cycle of 16% to 20%. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">5 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>TAXES </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The
provision for taxes, on an adjusted basis<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1,2</SUP>, was $17 million for the second quarter of 2015 and $51 million for the first half of 2015. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The effective tax rate for the second quarter, on an adjusted basis, was 11.6%, compared to 20.7% for the second quarter of 2014. As of the three-month period
ended June&nbsp;30, 2015, the provision for taxes, on an adjusted basis, did not and will no longer include any accruals for the Tax Receivable Agreement (TRA), due to the release of the valuation allowance for deferred tax assets and the related
recognition of a liability for our TRA obligation<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">2</SUP>. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The effective tax rate for the first half of
2015, on an adjusted basis, was 18.1%, compared to 20.9% for the first half of 2014. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>CAPITAL MANAGEMENT AND BALANCE SHEET </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Our primary capital management goals include managing debt and returning capital to shareholders through dividends and share repurchases. </I></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">For the second quarter of 2015, Lazard returned $80 million to shareholders, which included: $44 million in dividends; $35 million in share repurchases of our
Class&nbsp;A common stock; and $1 million in satisfaction of employee tax obligations in lieu of share issuances upon vesting of equity grants. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">For the
first half of 2015, Lazard returned $423 million to shareholders, which included: $203 million in dividends; $118 million in share repurchases of our Class&nbsp;A common stock; and $102 million in satisfaction of employee tax obligations in lieu of
share issuances upon vesting of equity grants. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">As of June&nbsp;30, 2015, we had repurchased 2.3&nbsp;million shares at an average price of $51.04 per
share during the first half of the year. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On July&nbsp;22, 2015, Lazard declared a quarterly dividend of $0.35 per share on its outstanding common stock.
The dividend is payable on August&nbsp;14, 2015, to stockholders of record on August&nbsp;3, 2015. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Lazard&#146;s financial position remains strong. As of
June&nbsp;30, 2015, our cash and cash equivalents were $701 million, and stockholders&#146; equity related to Lazard&#146;s interests was $810 million. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">*** </P>

<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">*** </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>ABOUT LAZARD </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Lazard, one of the world&#146;s preeminent financial advisory and asset management firms, operates from 43 cities across 27 countries in North America, Europe,
Asia, Australia, Central and South America. With origins dating to 1848, the firm provides advice on mergers and acquisitions, strategic matters, restructuring and capital structure, capital raising and corporate finance, as well as asset management
services to corporations, partnerships, institutions, governments and individuals. For more information on Lazard, please visit <U>www.lazard.com</U>. </P>

business-related information, and the posting of updates of assets under management in various hedge funds and mutual funds and other investment products managed by Lazard Asset Management LLC and its subsidiaries. Investors can link to Lazard and
its operating company websites through <U>www.lazard.com</U>. </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">*** </P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>ENDNOTES </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1 </SUP>A non-U.S. GAAP measure. See attached financial schedules and related notes for a detailed explanation of adjustments to corresponding U.S. GAAP results. We believe that presenting our results on an
adjusted basis, in addition to the U.S. GAAP results, is the most meaningful and useful way to compare our operating results across periods. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">2</SUP> In the second quarter of 2015, we released substantially all of our valuation allowance related to deferred tax assets, and we recognized a liability for our Tax Receivable Agreement (TRA)
obligation. As a result, the second quarter U.S. GAAP provision for income taxes included a benefit of approximately $1.2 billion, which was substantially offset by an accrual for our TRA obligation of approximately $962 million, resulting in a $237
million net benefit, or $1.78 (diluted) per share in the quarter. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">3</SUP> In the first half of 2015,
Lazard returned $423 million to shareholders, which included: $203 million in dividends; $118 million in share repurchases of our Class&nbsp;A common stock; and $102 million in satisfaction of employee tax obligations in lieu of share issuances upon
vesting of equity grants. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">4 </SUP>During the first quarter of 2015, Lazard Ltd&#146;s subsidiary Lazard
Group LLC completed a refinancing of a substantial majority of the outstanding $548 million of 6.85% senior notes maturing on June&nbsp;15, 2017 (the &#147;2017 Notes&#148;). A charge of $63 million related to the debt refinancing was comprised
primarily of an extinguishment loss of $60 million and other related costs. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">### </P>

<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(a)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">Selected Summary Financial Information are non-U.S. GAAP (&#147;non-GAAP&#148;) measures. Lazard believes that presenting results and measures on an adjusted basis in conjunction with U.S. GAAP measures provides the
most meaningful basis for comparison of its operating results across periods. </TD></TR></TABLE>

<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(b)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">A non-GAAP measure which excludes (i)&nbsp;revenue related to non-controlling interests (see (i)&nbsp;below), (ii)&nbsp;(gains)/losses related to the changes in the fair value of investments held in connection with
Lazard Fund Interests and other similar deferred compensation arrangements for which a corresponding equal amount is excluded from compensation&nbsp;&amp; benefits expense, (iii)&nbsp;for the three and six month periods ended June&nbsp;30, 2015,
private equity carried interest reduction (see (j)&nbsp;below), (iv)&nbsp;interest expense primarily related to corporate financing activities, and (v)&nbsp;for the three month period ended March&nbsp;31, 2015 and the six month period ended
June&nbsp;30, 2015, excess interest expense pertaining to Senior Debt refinancing (see (k)&nbsp;below). </TD></TR></TABLE>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(c)</TD>

compensation arrangements, and (ii)&nbsp;compensation and benefits related to noncontrolling interests (see (i)&nbsp;below). </TD></TR></TABLE>

(i)&nbsp;for the three month period ended March&nbsp;31, 2015 and the six month period ended June&nbsp;30, 2015, charges pertaining to Senior Debt refinancing, net of tax benefits (see (k)&nbsp;below), (ii)&nbsp;for the three and six month periods

<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(h)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">Effective tax rate is a non-GAAP measure based upon the U.S. GAAP rate with adjustments for the tax applicable to the non-GAAP adjustments to operating income, generally based upon the effective marginal tax rate in the
applicable jurisdiction of the adjustments. The computation is based on a quotient, the numerator of which is the provision (benefit) for income taxes of $17,067, $34,345 and $22,301 for the three month periods ended June&nbsp;30,
2015,&nbsp;March&nbsp;31, 2015, and June&nbsp;30, 2014, respectively, $51,412 and $44,086 for the six month periods ended June&nbsp;30, 2015 and 2014, respectively, and the denominator of which is pre-tax income of $147,327, $137,379 and $107,667
for the three month periods ended June&nbsp;30, 2015,&nbsp;March&nbsp;31, 2015, and June&nbsp;30, 2014, respectively, $284,706 and $210,727 for the six month periods ended June&nbsp;30, 2015 and 2014, respectively. The numerator also included a
provision pursuant to the tax receivable agreement (&#147;TRA&#148;) prior to the quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2015 (see (e)&nbsp;above) and excludes a release of deferred tax valuation allowance (see (l)&nbsp;below). </TD></TR></TABLE>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(k)</TD>

<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(m)</TD>
